Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
God's Transcendence of Time and Space
Sanusi negates temporal and spatial relations for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why temporal and spatial relations must be negated of God, and how the author uses analogy with space to make the point.

Core Idea
God is beyond time and space, so temporal and spatial relations are meaningless for Him.

In this passage, the author builds on previous discussions to definitively negate any temporal or spatial relationship with God. He draws a powerful analogy: just as a non-spatial being cannot have spatial relations, a non-temporal being cannot have temporal relations. This lesson introduces this foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's clear statement sink in.
2
Notice the parallel structure
The author negates temporal priority and concomitance, then immediately follows with the same for spatial relations. See how he builds the analogy.
The phrase 'كما أن ما لا يقبل المكان...' is key.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Ask yourself: If a being is not spatial, can it be 'above' or 'below'? Similarly, if not temporal, can it be 'before' or 'after'? This makes the negation self-evident.
This is a powerful argument from the nature of categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ثبت هذا قلنا: إما التقدم والتأخر الزماني فيجب نفيهما عن الباري تعالى، وكما لا يجوز أن يتقدم على العالم زمانًا لم يجز أن يكون مع العالم زمانًا، فإنا كما نفينا التقدم الزماني نفينا المعية الزمانية، ومثار الشبهة ومجال الخيال هاهنا، فإن فازت سفينة النظر عن هذه الغمرة فاز أهل الحق بقصب السبق في المسألة، فإن ما لا يقبل الزمان ولم يكن وجوده زمانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية الزمانية، كما أن ما لا يقبل المكان ولم يكن وجوده وجود مكانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية المكانية، فقول الخصم: إن العالم دائم الوجود إيهام بالزمان فيقال: يجوز أن يكون موجودان; أحدهما متقدم بالذات، والآخر متأخر بالذات، ويكونان معا في الزمان، فإن التقدم بالذات لا ينافي المعية في الزمان; كتقدم السبب على المسبب وحركة اليد على حركة المفتاح في الكم، لكن إذا كان وجودهما زمانين; فإما وجود لا يقبل الزمان أصلا كيف يطلق عليه معية بالزمان؟ وذلك فإن السبب والمسبب قد يكونان معا في المكان ويسبق أحدهما الآخر بالذات لكن إذا كان وجودهما مكانين، فإما وجود لا يقبل المكان أصلا فكيف يطلق عليه معية المكان؟ ونحن لا ننكر أن الوهم ليرتمي إلى مدة مقدرة قبل العالم، كما يرتمي إلى فضاء مقدر فوق العالم، وذلك وهم مجرد وخيال محض فلا فضاء ولا بينونة كما يقدره الكرامي، ولا زمان ولا مدة كما يقدره الوهمي، ولو قدر تقديراً عالم آخر فوق هذا
So if this is established, we say: As for temporal priority and posteriority, they must be negated of God Most High. And just as it is not permissible that He be prior to the world in time, so it is not permissible that He be with the world in time. For just as we negated temporal priority, we negate temporal concomitance. The source of confusion and the field of imagination is here. For if the ship of contemplation escapes this deep water, the people of truth will win the prize in this issue. For that which does not accept time and whose existence is not temporal, temporal priority, posteriority, and concomitance are not permissible for it, just as that which does not accept place and whose existence is not spatial, spatial priority, posteriority, and concomitance are not permissible for it. So the opponent's statement that the world is eternal in existence is an illusion of time. It is said: It is possible that two existents exist, one prior by essence and the other posterior by essence, and they are together in time. For priority by essence does not contradict concomitance in time; like the priority of the cause over the effect and the movement of the hand over the movement of the key in a lock. But if their existence is temporal, then if there is an existence that does not accept time at all, how can concomitance in time be attributed to it? That is because the cause and effect may be together in place and one precedes the other by essence, but if their existence is spatial, then if there is an existence that does not accept place at all, how can spatial concomitance be attributed to it? And we do not deny that imagination reaches out to an estimated duration before the world, just as it reaches out to an estimated space above the world. But that is mere imagination and pure fantasy: there is no space and no separation as the Karramiyya imagine, and no time and no duration as the fantasy imagines. And if one were to estimate another world above this...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is beyond time and space. The author builds on the earlier discussion of priority. He first states that if the previous points are established, then temporal priority and posteriority must be negated of God. Furthermore, just as temporal priority is negated, so is temporal concomitance (i.e., being together in time). He then analogizes to place: if something does not accept place as spatial, then spatial relations are negated. The author addresses an opponent who claims the world is eternal, which implies temporal priority for God. He replies that it is possible for two things to exist where one is prior by essence and the other posterior by essence, yet both are together in time, like cause and effect. However, this applies only when both are temporal. For God, who does not accept time, temporal concomitance is meaningless. He then discusses the imagination that posits a time before the world or a space above it, stating this is pure fantasy. He specifically mentions the Karramiyya who imagine a separation (bainuna) and others who imagine time. The passage ends mid-sentence suggesting another world above this one is similarly imaginary.

Key Terms
تَقَدُّم
تَأَخُّر
مَعِيَّة
زَمَان
مَكَان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God is in time or space, or has temporal/spatial relations with creation.
Correction: The author shows that temporal and spatial categories apply only to temporal/spatial beings, not to God who is beyond both.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is negated for God along with temporal priority?
A) Essential priority
B) Spatial priority
C) Temporal concomitance
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
God is beyond time and space, so all temporal and spatial relations—priority, posteriority, togetherness—are inapplicable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you conceive of God as 'eternal,' do you unconsciously imagine Him existing for an immense duration rather than beyond time entirely? How does the negation of temporal priority challenge your mental image, and what must you do to correct it in your worship?
?
Your daily prayers are tied to specific times. How does knowing that God is beyond time change the way you approach the punctuality of salah? Does it transform it into a moment of connection with the Timeless, or do you treat it as a routine task? What concrete step can you take this week to make that shift?
?
If spatial relations are negated for God, then He is not literally 'above' the heavens. Do you still rely on spatial imagery when supplicating? How does this lesson compel you to refine your understanding of His nearness, and what practice can you adopt to internalize that He is beyond all spatial concepts?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
6 min
Refuting the Illusion of Time Before the World
Sanusi refutes the opponent's temporal illusion and dismisses imaginary time/space.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the opponent's claim that God's eternity implies temporal priority, and why the imagination's positing of time or space before/above the world is mere fantasy.

Core Idea
Eternity does not mean temporal priority; God is timeless, and imagined durations are illusions.

The author now addresses a crucial objection: if the world is eternal, doesn't that imply God is temporally prior? He answers with a clear distinction between essential priority and temporal priority, using the cause-effect example. He then exposes the imagination's tendency to project time and space where they do not exist, warning against such fantasies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Read the opening line where the author mentions the opponent's statement that the world is eternal. Understand the implied temporal priority.
The opponent likely thinks that an eternal world alongside God makes God temporally prior.
2
Understand the author's counter
The author says two things can exist together in time while one is essentially prior. The cause-effect example (hand and key) clarifies this.
Essential priority does not require temporal priority.
3
Apply the analogy to God
The distinction only applies when both are temporal. For a non-temporal being like God, even 'together in time' is meaningless.
The author extends the same logic to spatial relations.
4
Recognize the rejection of fantasy
The author dismisses imagined time before the world or space above it as mere imagination and pure fantasy, naming the Karramiyya as an example.
This warns against letting the mind project categories where they do not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ثبت هذا قلنا: إما التقدم والتأخر الزماني فيجب نفيهما عن الباري تعالى، وكما لا يجوز أن يتقدم على العالم زمانًا لم يجز أن يكون مع العالم زمانًا، فإنا كما نفينا التقدم الزماني نفينا المعية الزمانية، ومثار الشبهة ومجال الخيال هاهنا، فإن فازت سفينة النظر عن هذه الغمرة فاز أهل الحق بقصب السبق في المسألة، فإن ما لا يقبل الزمان ولم يكن وجوده زمانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية الزمانية، كما أن ما لا يقبل المكان ولم يكن وجوده وجود مكانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية المكانية، فقول الخصم: إن العالم دائم الوجود إيهام بالزمان فيقال: يجوز أن يكون موجودان; أحدهما متقدم بالذات، والآخر متأخر بالذات، ويكونان معا في الزمان، فإن التقدم بالذات لا ينافي المعية في الزمان; كتقدم السبب على المسبب وحركة اليد على حركة المفتاح في الكم، لكن إذا كان وجودهما زمانين; فإما وجود لا يقبل الزمان أصلا كيف يطلق عليه معية بالزمان؟ وذلك فإن السبب والمسبب قد يكونان معا في المكان ويسبق أحدهما الآخر بالذات لكن إذا كان وجودهما مكانين، فإما وجود لا يقبل المكان أصلا فكيف يطلق عليه معية المكان؟ ونحن لا ننكر أن الوهم ليرتمي إلى مدة مقدرة قبل العالم، كما يرتمي إلى فضاء مقدر فوق العالم، وذلك وهم مجرد وخيال محض فلا فضاء ولا بينونة كما يقدره الكرامي، ولا زمان ولا مدة كما يقدره الوهمي، ولو قدر تقديراً عالم آخر فوق هذا
So if this is established, we say: As for temporal priority and posteriority, they must be negated of God Most High. And just as it is not permissible that He be prior to the world in time, so it is not permissible that He be with the world in time. For just as we negated temporal priority, we negate temporal concomitance. The source of confusion and the field of imagination is here. For if the ship of contemplation escapes this deep water, the people of truth will win the prize in this issue. For that which does not accept time and whose existence is not temporal, temporal priority, posteriority, and concomitance are not permissible for it, just as that which does not accept place and whose existence is not spatial, spatial priority, posteriority, and concomitance are not permissible for it. So the opponent's statement that the world is eternal in existence is an illusion of time. It is said: It is possible that two existents exist, one prior by essence and the other posterior by essence, and they are together in time. For priority by essence does not contradict concomitance in time; like the priority of the cause over the effect and the movement of the hand over the movement of the key in a lock. But if their existence is temporal, then if there is an existence that does not accept time at all, how can concomitance in time be attributed to it? That is because the cause and effect may be together in place and one precedes the other by essence, but if their existence is spatial, then if there is an existence that does not accept place at all, how can spatial concomitance be attributed to it? And if one were to estimate another world above this...

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is beyond time and space. The author builds on the earlier discussion of priority. He first states that if the previous points are established, then temporal priority and posteriority must be negated of God. Furthermore, just as temporal priority is negated, so is temporal concomitance (i.e., being together in time). He specifically mentions the Karramiyya who imagine a separation (bainuna) and others who imagine time. The passage ends mid-sentence suggesting another world above this one is similarly imaginary.

A) It is a valid argument

God is timeless, so temporal priority and concomitance are inapplicable; imagined time before the world is pure fantasy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God 'before' creation, do you catch yourself picturing a long stretch of time? How does this lesson show that such a picture is an illusion, and what does that demand from your heart in terms of how you relate to a timeless Creator?
?
Your mind naturally wants to locate God in a timeline or a place. Where in your daily life do you treat God as if He is bound by your schedule or your problems? What would change if you truly believed He is beyond time, unconstrained by your lack of patience or your sense of urgency?
?
If all your mental images of God and His relation to the world are ultimately products of your imagination—like the Karramiyya's imagined space—are you willing to let go of those comfortable images and embrace the pure transcendence that the author describes? What is one concrete thought or habit you need to change to stop imagining God within created limits?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
6 min
Negating Temporal and Spatial Relations from God
The author negates temporal and spatial priority and simultaneity from God and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why temporal and spatial relations cannot be attributed to God, and how the author refutes the opponent's analogy of essential priority with temporal simultaneity.

Core Idea
Time and space are created; God transcends both, so no temporal or spatial relations apply to Him.

This passage tackles a central theological issue: how does the eternal God relate to the temporal world? Some might argue that God could be essentially prior yet coexist in time, like cause and effect. The author shows this analogy fails because God is not subject to time at all. Let's examine his argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical flow: negation of temporal relations, then spatial analogy, then objection and response.
2
Identify the negations
The author negates temporal priority, temporal simultaneity, and spatial relations from God. How does he justify these negations?
He uses the principle that what does not admit time cannot have temporal relations.
3
Examine the opponent's objection
The opponent brings an analogy: two existents can be one prior in essence yet simultaneous in time (like cause and effect). Why does this seem to challenge the negation?
The challenge is that if God is essentially prior, He might still be with the world in time.
4
Understand the author's refutation
The author points out that the analogy requires both existents to be temporal. Since God is not temporal, the analogy fails. Similarly for space.
This is a classic disanalogy argument in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ثبت هذا قلنا: إما التقدم والتأخر الزماني فيجب نفيهما عن الباري تعالى، وكما لا يجوز أن يتقدم على العالم زمانًا لم يجز أن يكون مع العالم زمانًا، فإنا كما نفينا التقدم الزماني نفينا المعية الزمانية، ومثار الشبهة ومجال الخيال هاهنا، فإن فازت سفينة النظر عن هذه الغمرة فاز أهل الحق بقصب السبق في المسألة، فإن ما لا يقبل الزمان ولم يكن وجوده زمانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية الزمانية، كما أن ما لا يقبل المكان ولم يكن وجوده مكانيا لم يجز عليه التقدم والتأخر والمعية المكانية، فقول الخصم : إن العالم دايم الوجود إيهام بالزمان فيقال: يجوز أن يكون موجودان؛ أحدهما متقدم بالذات، والآخر متأخر بالذات، ويكونان معا في الزمان، فإن التقدم بالذات لا ينافي المعية في الزمان؛ كتقدم السبب على المسبب وحركة اليد على حركة المفتاح في الكم، لكن إذا كان وجودهما زمانين؛ فإما وجود لا يقبل الزمان أصلا كيف يطلق عليه معية بالزمان؟ وذلك فإن السبب والمسبب قد يكونان معا في المكان ويسبق أحدهما الآخر بالذات لكن إذا كان وجودهما مكانين، فإما وجود لا يقبل المكان أصلا فكيف يطلق عليه معية المكان؟
When this is established, we say: As for temporal priority and posteriority, it is obligatory to negate them from God Most High. And just as it is not permissible for Him to be temporally prior to the world, it is not permissible for Him to be temporally simultaneous with the world. For just as we negated temporal priority, we negate temporal simultaneity. The source of the doubt and the field of imagination is here. If the ship of reflection escapes this whirlpool, the people of truth win the race in this issue. For that which does not admit time and whose existence is not temporal cannot have temporal priority, posteriority, or simultaneity. Just as that which does not admit space and whose existence is not spatial cannot have spatial priority, posteriority, or simultaneity. So the opponent's statement that the world is eternal in existence is an illusion with time. It is said: It is possible for two existents to exist, one prior in essence and the other posterior in essence, and they be simultaneous in time, for essential priority does not conflict with temporal simultaneity, like the priority of the cause over the effect and the movement of the hand over the movement of the key in the lock. But if their existence is temporal, then how can a being that does not admit time at all be said to have temporal simultaneity? Similarly, the cause and effect may be simultaneous in space while one precedes the other in essence, but if their existence is spatial, then how can a being that does not admit space at all be said to have spatial simultaneity?
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation concerning God's relation to time and space. The author begins by asserting that temporal priority and posteriority must be negated from God, and also temporal simultaneity, just as spatial relations are negated. He identifies this as the root of doubt and imagination. He then refutes the opponent's objection: the opponent suggests that two things can coexist in time while one is essentially prior (like cause and effect), so perhaps God could be essentially prior to the world yet coexist in time. The author replies by pointing out that this analogy requires both existents to be temporal; but God's existence is not temporal at all. Therefore, applying temporal simultaneity to God is invalid. The same point is made regarding spatial relations. This is a classic kalam argument using analogy and disanalogy.

Key Terms
التقدم الزماني
التأخر الزماني
المعية الزمانية
التقدم بالذات
المعية المكانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because cause and effect can be simultaneous in time with essential priority, God could similarly be with the world in time.
Correction: The author shows this fails because the analogy assumes both existents are temporal, but God's existence is not temporal at all.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the opponent's analogy of cause and effect (essential priority with temporal simultaneity) fail when applied to God?
A) Because cause and effect are always separate in time.
B) Because the analogy assumes both existents are temporal, but God is not temporal.
C) Because the opponent does not believe in causation.
D) Because spatial priority is more relevant.

Key Takeaway
Because God transcends time and space, no temporal or spatial relations—priority, posteriority, or simultaneity—can apply to Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is beyond time, then your past sins are not 'far away' from Him. How does this immediacy affect your repentance today? Will you turn to Him now as if no time separates you?
?
You often think of God as 'before' or 'after' events in your life. But this lesson says He transcends time. How does this change the way you should speak about His actions in your prayers?
?
If God is not in time, then your entire life is present to Him in one 'now'. Does this make you more aware of His constant witness? What will you change in your behavior knowing that no moment is hidden?

Divine Transcendence
beginner
5 min
The Impossibility of Infinite Bodies in Time and Space
Shahrastani refutes illusions of infinite duration and space, concluding God was alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imagination of infinite time and space before the world is logically impossible, and how this leads to the conclusion that God was alone with no simultaneity in any sense.

Core Idea
God's transcendence means He is outside all time and space, and was alone before creation.

This passage from Shahrastani's Nihayat al-Aqdam tackles a fundamental theological confusion: the tendency to imagine infinite duration or space extending beyond the world. The author shows that such imagination is pure fantasy and that rigorous demonstration proves the impossibility of infinite extension in space or time. This sets the stage for affirming that God existed alone before creation, with no co-existence in any form.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the illusion of infinite time and space
Read the opening lines where the author acknowledges that the mind leaps to imagine a duration before the world and a space above it. Notice how he dismisses these as pure illusion.
The author uses 'وهم' (imagination) and 'خيال' (fantasy) to stress that these are not real.
2
Understand the proof of impossibility
Follow the argument that supposing another world above or before does not entail actual infinity of bodies or motions. The author claims demonstration proves impossibility of infinite extension and infinite duration.
Look for the phrases 'تبين بالبرهان' (it has been proven by demonstration).
3
Grasp the conclusion that God was alone
The passage culminates in 'كان الله ولم يكن معه شيء' (And God was and there was nothing with Him). Understand how the author systematically negates all forms of simultaneity—in essence, existence, and spatiotemporal rank.
The term 'معية' (simultaneity) is key; the author denies it from every angle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لا ننكر أن الوهم ليرتمي إلى مدة مقدرة قبل العالم، كما يرتمي إلى فضاء مقدر فوق العالم، وذلك وهم مجرد وخيال محض فلا فضاء ولا بينونة كما يقدره الكرامي، ولا زمان ولا مدة كما يقدره الوهمي، ولو قدر تقديراً عالم آخر فوق هذا العالم لم يؤد ذلك تجويز عوالم هي أجسام لا تتناهى؛ إذ قد تبين بالبرهان استحالة بعدٍ لا يتناهى في الملا والخلا وكذلك لو قدر تقديرًا عالم آخر قبل هذا العالم لم يؤد ذلك إلى تجويز عوالم هي متحركات لا تتناهى؛ إذ تبين بالبرهان استحالة مدة وعدة لا تتناهى، فرجع الخلاف إذا إلى استحالة وجود جسم لا يتناهى بعداً، وبيان استحالة وجود أجسام لا تتناهى زمانًا، فإن الخصم يسلم التقدم والتأخر في المعية، فإذا سلم التقدم نقول : لا يلزم من تقدير جسم لا يتناهى بعداً وإن كان مستحيلا أن يكون مع الباري تعالى بالمكان، كذلك لم يلزم من تقدير حركات لا تتناهى زمانًا أن تكون مع الباري تعالى بالزمان؛ فإنه تعالى غير قابل للزمان والمكان وكان الله ولم يكن معه شيء؛ إذ لم تكن معية بالذات ولا بالوجود، ولا بالرتبة المكانية والزمانية، ولم يلزم من إطلاق كونه موجدا أن يكون في الوجود، أولا لزم من إطلاق كونه موجبًا أن يكون الموجب معه في الوجود، فإن الوجود المستفاد لا يكون مع الوجود المفيد، وكان المعية من كل وجه، وعلى كل معنى من الأقسام منفيا عنه، سواء أطلقناها في قسم واحد أو في قسمين مركبين
We do not deny that the imagination leaps to a supposed duration before the world, as it leaps to a supposed space above the world. That is pure illusion and mere fantasy. There is no space or interval as the Karrāmī imagines, and no time or duration as the imaginary one posits. If one supposes another world above this world, that would not entail allowing infinite bodies, since it has been proven by demonstration the impossibility of infinite extension in filled and empty space. Likewise, if one supposes another world before this world, that would not entail allowing infinite moving bodies, since it has been proven by demonstration the impossibility of infinite duration and number. Thus the disagreement reduces to the impossibility of a body infinite in extension, and the demonstration of the impossibility of bodies infinite in time. For the opponent concedes priority and posteriority in simultaneity. If he concedes priority, we say: From the supposition of a body infinite in extension, even if impossible, it does not follow that it is with God Most High in place. Similarly, from the supposition of infinite movements in time, it does not follow that they are with God Most High in time. For He Most High is not receptive to time or place. And God was and there was nothing with Him; there was no simultaneity in essence, nor in existence, nor in spatial or temporal rank. And from the attribution of His being an originator (mūjid), it does not follow that He is in existence, otherwise from the attribution of His being a necessitator (mūjib), it would follow that the necessitator is with Him in existence. For derived existence is not together with the existence that bestows. Thus simultaneity in every respect and in every sense of the categories is negated from Him, whether we apply it in a single category or in two combined categories.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the opponent's imagination of infinite time and space and a proof that God is absolutely transcendent. The author acknowledges that the mind imagines a duration before the world and a space above the world, but these are illusions. He argues that positing another world above or before does not entail an actual infinite series of bodies or motions, because the impossibility of infinite spatial extension (in plenum or void) and infinite temporal duration has been established by demonstration. The real dispute thus reduces to the impossibility of infinite bodies in extension or in time. The opponent accepts that there is essential priority and posteriority in simultaneity; given that, the author states that even if one posits an infinite body (spatially) or infinite motions (temporally), it does not force them to be with God in space or time, because God is not receptive to space or time. The climax is the famous phrase 'And God was and there was nothing with Him' – meaning no simultaneity in essence, existence, or any spatiotemporal rank. The author also adds that attributing to God the act of origination does not imply that He is in existence alongside the originated, otherwise the same would apply to the attributive necessitator. Thus all forms of simultaneity are negated from God.

مدة مقدرة
فضاء مقدر
لا يتناهى

كان الله ولم يكن معه شيء
معية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because the world is not created in time, it must be simultaneous with God in some sense.
Correction: The author shows that God's existence is wholly outside time and space; there is no simultaneity in essence, existence, or spatiotemporal rank.

Checkpoint

D) That the world is not created by God.

Key Takeaway
God was alone with no simultaneity in essence, existence, or spatiotemporal rank.

Two Kinds of Eternity and Refutation of Co-Eternity
Juwayni clarifies the two meanings of eternity and refutes the world's co-eternity with God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between essential (non-temporal) eternity and temporal duration, and why the world cannot be eternal with God.

Core Idea
God's eternity is timeless and essential; any other eternity is merely temporal.

Juwayni begins by critiquing those who claim the world is eternal with God, arguing they misuse the word 'eternity' (dawām) homonymously. He then clarifies two fundamentally distinct meanings: God's eternity is essential, non-temporal, and necessary, while the world's duration is temporal, having a beginning and subject to change. Finally, he presents a logical reductio showing that if the world were eternal with God's eternity, it would either make God temporal or make the world necessary—both impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Juwayni's critical tone and logical flow come through.
Notice the rhetorical question at the beginning.
2
Identify the two definitions of eternity
Find where Juwayni defines God's eternity (essential, non-temporal) and the world's duration (temporal, with beginning). Note the distinct attributes he assigns to each.
God is 'First without a first, Last without a last'; the world 'has a beginning'.
3
Understand the reductio argument
Trace the conditional argument: If the two eternities were the same, then either God's existence would be temporal or the world's existence would be essential. Both are false, so the premise is false.
4
Connect to the broader proof
Note that Juwayni says this falsehood becomes fully clear when we prove the impossibility of an infinite regress of events and infinite existents. This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فما معنى قولكم : الجايز دايم الوجود بالواجب أو مع الواجب ، أو قدرتم دوام وجود الباري تعالى زمانيا ممتداً مع الأزمنة غير المتناهية، كما توهمتم وجود العالم زمانيا ممتداً في أزمنة لا تتناهى وبئس الوهم وهمكم في الدوامين، فكأنكم أخذتم لفظ الدوام بالاشتراك المحض؟ أما دوام وجود الباري تعالى فمعناه أنه واجب لذاته وبذاته، ولا يتطرق إليه جواز ولا عدم بوجه من الوجوه، فهو الأول بلا أول كان قبله، والآخر بلا آخر كان بعده، وأوله آخره، وآخره أوله؛ أي ليس وجوده زمانيا. وأما العالم فله أول ودوامه دوام زماني يتطرق إليه الجواز والعدم والقلة والكثرة، والاستمرار والانقطاع فلو كان دايم الوجود بدوام الباري كان الباري دايم الوجود بدوام العالم، فلو كان الدوامان بمعنى واحد فيلزم أن يكون وجود الباري تعالى زمانيا ، أو وجود العالم ذاتيا ، وكلا الوجهين باطل، فبطل قولكم : إن العالم دايم الوجود بالواجب، وإنما يتضح هذا البطلان كل الوضوح إذا أثبتنا استحالة حوادث لا أول لها ووجود موجودات لا تتناهى.
So what is the meaning of your statement: 'the possible is eternal in existence by the Necessary or with the Necessary'? Or you supposed the duration of the existence of the Exalted Creator as temporal, extended with endless times, just as you imagined the existence of the world as temporal, extended in endless times? How bad is the imagination of your two eternities! As if you took the word 'eternity' (dawām) by pure homonymy. As for the duration of the existence of the Exalted Creator, its meaning is that He is necessary in Himself and by Himself, and possibility and non-existence do not affect Him in any way, so He is the First without a first before Him, and the Last without a last after Him, and His first is His last, and His last is His first; that is, His existence is not temporal. And as for the world, it has a beginning and its duration is a temporal duration, affected by possibility and non-existence, paucity and multiplicity, continuity and discontinuity. So if it were eternal in existence by the eternity of the Creator, then the Creator would be eternal in existence by the duration of the world. So if the two eternities were one meaning, then it would necessitate that the existence of the Exalted Creator be temporal, or the existence of the world be essential; and both aspects are false. So your statement that the world is eternal in existence by the Necessary is false. And this falsehood becomes fully clear when we establish the impossibility of events with no beginning and of existents that are infinite.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author questions the opponent's claim that the possible is eternal with God, criticizing them for using the word 'eternity' (dawām) homonymously. He then clarifies two distinct meanings: God's eternity is essential, necessary, non-temporal (He is the First without a beginning, the Last without an end, and His existence is not temporal). The world's eternity, on the other hand, is temporal, having a beginning, and subject to possibility, non-existence, and change. If the world were eternal with God's eternity, it would either make God temporal or make the world necessary—both false. Therefore the claim is false, and this will become fully clear when the impossibility of an infinite regress of events and infinite existents is proven.

Correction: Juwayni shows that 'eternity' for God means essential, non-temporal necessity, while for the world it means temporal duration with a beginning. They are homonymous.

Key Takeaway
God's eternity is essential, timeless, and necessary; the world's duration is temporal and contingent—they are not the same, so the world cannot be co-eternal with God.

For example, do you think of God's 'love' or 'justice' as just a bigger version of human love or justice? What step will you take this week to purify your understanding of a divine attribute?

Why God is Not Subject to Time
Author presents and begins refuting the Dahriyya's temporal dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Dahriyya's objection about the delay of the world is invalid because temporal categories do not apply to God.

Core Idea
God’s existence is beyond time—no priority, delay, or simultaneity.

The Dahriyya (materialists) argued that if the world is originated, its existence must be delayed from God, leading to absurd consequences. The author responds by pointing out that the entire objection is built on a mistaken assumption: that God's existence is within time. This lesson unpacks their objection and the author’s initial refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical dilemma the Dahriyya attempt to force.
The objection presents a division into four possibilities.
2
Identify the four-fold division
Trace the branches: delay without a period, delay with a finite period, delay with an infinite period. Each leads to a supposed absurdity.
The author will later reject the division entirely.
3
Understand the critique of formulation
The author first attacks the 'formulation' (wad'): the claim of temporal delay is not conceded because God is not subject to time.
This is a fundamental theological point: God is beyond temporal relations.
4
See why the division fails
Since God does not accept temporal periods, the entire division into 'by a period or not' is invalid. The objection collapses.
The answer is incomplete here but the core refutation is already clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه الدهرية قالوا : إذا قلتم : إن العالم محدث بعد أن لم يكن فقد تأخر وجوده عن وجود الباري تعالى فلا يخلو إما أن يتأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة، فإن تأخر لا بمدة فقد قارن وجوده وجود الباري تعالى وإن تأخر بمدة فلا يخلو إما أن تأخر بمدة متناهية أو بمدة غير متناهية، فإن تأخر بمدة متناهية فقد وجب تناهي وجود الباري سبحانه، وإن تأخر بمدة غير متناهية فنفرض في تلك المدة موجودات لا تتناهى، فإنه إن لم يمتنع مدة لا تتناهى لم يمتنع عدة لا تتناهى. والجواب : قلنا هذا الكلام غير مستقيم وضعا وتقسيما؛ أما الوضع فقولكم : لو كان العالم محدثا كان وجوده متأخراً، فإن عنيتم به التأخر بالزمان فغير مُسلم ، فإنا قد بينا أن التقدم والتأخر والمعية الزمانية تمتنع في حق الباري سبحانه. وعلى هذا لم يصح بنا التقسيم عليه أنه متأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة، فإن ما لا يقبل المدة ذاتًا ووجودًا لا يقال له : تقدم أو تأخر، أو قارن بمدة أو لا بمدة، فأحلتم علينا
The doubt of the materialists (Dahriyya): They said: If you say that the world is originated (muhdath) after it was not, then its existence is delayed (ta'akhkhara) from the existence of God Most High. So it must either be delayed by a period (mudda) or not by a period. If it is delayed not by a period, then its existence coincided with the existence of God Most High. And if it is delayed by a period, then it must either be delayed by a finite period or by an infinite period. If it is delayed by a finite period, then the finitude of the existence of God Most High becomes necessary. And if it is delayed by an infinite period, then we suppose in that period existents that are infinite, for if a period that is infinite is not impossible, then a number that is infinite is not impossible. And the answer: We say: This speech is not sound in terms of formulation (wad') and division (taqsim). As for the formulation, your statement: If the world is originated, its existence is delayed—if you mean by it temporal delay, it is not conceded, for we have already explained that priority (taqaddum), posteriority (ta'akhkhur), and temporal simultaneity (mu'iyya zamaniyya) are impossible with respect to God Most High. On this basis, the division upon Him that He is delayed by a period or not by a period is not valid for us, for that which does not accept a period in essence and existence cannot be said to have priority, posteriority, or simultaneity by a period or not by a period. Thus you have made an error against us.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage records an objection from the Dahriyya (materialist/eternalist school) against the Islamic doctrine that the world is originated (muhdath). The objection attempts to force a dilemma regarding the temporal relation between God and the world: if the world began after not existing, then its existence is 'delayed' relative to God. This delay must either involve a period of time or not. If no period, then the world coexisted eternally with God, contradicting its being originated. If a period, then that period is either finite or infinite. If finite, then God's existence is bounded by time. If infinite, then there must be an infinite number of existents in that period, which the opponent thinks is impossible. The author's answer, though cut off in this window, begins by rejecting the 'formulation' (wad') and 'division' (taqsim) of the objection. He argues that the terms 'delay' (ta'akhkhur), 'priority' (taqaddum), and 'temporal simultaneity' do not apply to God, because God is not subject to time (mudda). Since God's essence and existence do not accept temporal periods, the entire division into 'by a period or not by a period' is invalid. The author asserts that this has been proven earlier (in the book), showing that the objection is fundamentally misguided. The incomplete answer likely continues to refute the implications of an infinite period on other grounds.

المدة
التقدم
التأخر
المعية الزمانية
الوضع
التقسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's existence before the world involves temporal priority.
Correction: In kalam, God is beyond time, so temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity do not apply to Him.

Checkpoint

B) Because God does not accept temporal periods in His essence and existence.
C) Because the world's existence is not delayed but simultaneous.
D) Because the period must be finite to avoid an infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
The Dahriyya objection fails because it wrongly applies temporal categories to God, who is beyond time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Dahriyya's error was applying human temporal categories to God. In what subtle ways do you still think of God as having human-like limitations—like being slow, in a hurry, or distant in time? Confess one such thought and ask God to purify your understanding.
?
God's existence does not accept periods. That means His love for you is not 'new' or 'old' — it is eternal and beyond time. Does your heart rest in that timeless love, or do you still measure His care by your circumstances? Commit to trust Him today.

Meaning of Divine Infinity: Oneness, Not Extension
Author explains divine infinity as oneness and indivisibility via analogy of power and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the infinity of Allah's essence means His oneness and indivisibility, not boundless spatial extension.

Core Idea
Divine infinity is about indivisible oneness, not endless extension.

When theologians say that Allah's essence is infinite, they do not mean that He extends infinitely in space. Instead, they mean that He is one and cannot be divided. This passage from al-Shahrastani clarifies this by first discussing the infinity of divine power and knowledge, and then concluding that the same logic applies to the essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style and the analogy used.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage asserts that divine infinity means oneness and indivisibility. Find the exact phrase where this is stated.
The phrase 'واحد لا يقبل الانقسام' is central.
3
Understand the analogy
The author first discusses power and knowledge to illustrate that infinity is not about extension or number. See how that leads to the conclusion about the essence.
This analogy helps prevent the misconception of spatial infinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك لصلاحية القدرة أن يقدر بها على كل ما يصح أن يقدر عليه " يُقال : إن القدرة لا تتناهى فلا القدرة ولا العلم أمر بسيط ذاهب في الجهات لا يتناهى ولا المعلومات والمقدورات أعداد كثيرة لا تتناهى، وهكذا ينبغي أن تفهم من معنى قولنا : ذات الباري سبحانه لا تتناهى )؛ أي هو واحد لا يقبل الانقسام بوجه من الوجوه ، فلا يتطرق إليه نهاية بوجه من الوجوه.
And likewise, the suitability of power is that by it one is able to do everything that it is valid to be capable of. It is said: power is not finite. So neither power nor knowledge is a simple thing extending in directions without end, nor are the known things and the things capable of being done numerous without end. And thus you should understand from the meaning of our saying: the Essence of the Creator, exalted, is not finite; that is, He is one, not divisible in any way, so no termination reaches Him in any respect.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage defines the meaning of God's infinity. The author first explains that divine power is suitable for all possible objects of power, and that power is not finite. Similarly, divine knowledge is not a simple thing extending in directions without limit; nor are the objects of knowledge and power endless in number. Then the author instructs that this is how one should understand the statement 'the Essence of the Creator is not finite': it means He is one, indivisible in every respect, and thus no termination applies to Him. The key point is that God's infinity is not quantitative extension but oneness and indivisibility.

Key Terms

ذات الباري
واحد لا يقبل الانقسام

Correction: The passage clarifies that infinity of the essence means oneness and indivisibility, not extension or number.

Key Takeaway
Allah's infinity means He is one and indivisible, not that He is vast in size or number.

The Dahriyya's Objection on the Temporality of the World
Dahriyya present a dilemma on creation's delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the materialist argument that the creation of the world implies a temporal delay in God's existence, and the four-part partition they propose.

Core Idea
The Dahriyya argue that if the world began, its existence must be delayed from God's.

The Dahriyya, ancient materialists, reject the idea that the world is created. They present a dilemma: if the world is originated after not existing, its existence must be delayed relative to God. This delay must either be by a duration or not, leading to absurdities. In this lesson, we will examine their argument carefully to understand its structure before seeing the author's refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage of the Dahriyya's argument once. Then read the translation to grasp the logical flow.
Notice the use of 'if…then' structure.
2
Identify the four possibilities
The argument divides the delay into two main branches: with or without a duration. Each branch is then subdivided. List all four possibilities and their implications.
This is a classic case of exhaustive division (taqsim).
3
Consider the conclusion
The Dahriyya conclude that all possibilities lead to absurdity: either God's existence becomes finite, or an infinite number of past events is required. Reflect on why this would be a problem for theists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه الدهرية قالوا: إذا قلتم: إن العالم محدث بعد أن لم يكن فقد تأخر وجوده عن وجود الباري تعالى فلا يخلو إما أن يتأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة، فإن تأخر لا بمدة فقد قارن وجوده وجود الباري تعالى وإن تأخر بمدة فلا يخلو إما أن تأخر بمدة متناهية أو بمدة غير متناهية، فإن تأخر بمدة متناهية فقد وجب تناهي وجود الباري سبحانه، وإن تأخر بمدة غير متناهية فنفرض في تلك المدة موجودات لا تتناهى، فإنه إن لم يمتنع مدة لا تتناهى لم يمتنع عدة لا تتناهى.
والجواب: قلنا هذا الكلام غير مستقيم وضعا وتقسيما؛ أما الوضع فقولكم: لو كان العالم محدثا كان وجوده متأخراً، فإن عنيتم به التأخر بالزمان فغير مُسلم، فإنا قد بينا أن التقدم والتأخر والمعية الزمانية تمتنع في حق الباري سبحانه. وعلى هذا لم يصح بنا التقسيم عليه أنه متأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة، فإن ما لا يقبل المدة ذانا ووجودا لا يقال له: تقدم أو تأخر، أو قارن بمدة أو لا بمدة، فأحلتم علينا تقدمًا وتأخرًا ومعية زمانية للباري تعالى، وإذا منعنا ذلك ألزمتم علينا مقارنة في الوجود وذلك تلبيس، فإنا إذا منعنا التقدم والتأخر الزماني منعنا المقارنة الزمانية، بل وجود الباري تعالى لا يقال: متقدم بالزمان، كما لا يقال أيضا: فوق بالمكان، ولا يقال: مقارن بالزمان كما لا يقال: مجاور للعالم بالمكان، وإن عنيتم بالتأخر في الوجود؛ أي الموجد مفيد الوجود، والموجد مستفيد الوجود، والموجد لا أول لوجوده، والموجد له أول فهو مسلم، ولا يصح أيضًا بنا التقسيم عليه أنه تأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة.
فإن قيل: لا بد من نسبة ما بين الموجد والموجد، وإذا تحققت النسبة فبمدة متناهية أو غير متناهية.
قلنا: ولا بد من نفي النسبة بين الموجد والموجد؛ إذ لو تحققت النسبة بمدة متناهية أو غير متناهية كان وجوده زمانيا قابلا للتغير والحركة، أليس لو قال القائل: ما نسبة واحد منا حيث حدث، وله أول كان السؤال محالا، أليس لو قال القائل: ما نسبة العالم منه تعالى حيث وجد وله نهاية أفيباينه أو يجاوره، فإن باينه أفبخلا[؟] أو بينونة تتناهى أم لا تتناهى، كان السؤال محالا، كذلك نقول في المدة فإن الجزئي كالكلي والزمان كالمكان.
The Dahriyya raise an objection saying: If you say that the world is temporally originated after it was not, then its existence is delayed from the existence of God, exalted. Then it is inevitable either that it is delayed by a duration or not by a duration. If it is delayed not by a duration, then its existence coexisted with the existence of God, exalted. And if it is delayed by a duration, then it is inevitable either that it is delayed by a finite duration or by an infinite duration. If it is delayed by a finite duration, then the finitude of God's existence is necessitated. And if it is delayed by an infinite duration, then we suppose in that duration existents without end, for if a duration without end is not impossible, then a number without end is not impossible.
The answer: We say: This speech is not sound in formulation and division. As for the formulation: your saying 'if the world is temporally originated, its existence was delayed' – if you mean by it temporal delay, it is not granted, for we have already demonstrated that temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity are impossible with respect to God, exalted. And on this basis, the division into it being delayed by a duration or not by a duration does not apply to us, because that which does not accept duration in essence and existence cannot be said to be prior, posterior, or coexistent with a duration or not with a duration. So you have foisted upon us temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity for God, exalted. And when we deny that, you impose upon us coexistence in existence, and that is obfuscation, for when we deny temporal priority and posteriority, we deny temporal coexistence. Rather, the existence of God, exalted, is not said to be prior in time, just as it is not said to be above in place, nor is it said to be coexistent in time, just as it is not said to be adjacent to the world in place. And if you mean by delay in existence, i.e., the Creator is the bestower of existence and the created is the recipient of existence, and the Creator has no beginning to His existence, and the created has a beginning, then it is granted, and the division into it being delayed by a duration or not by a duration does not apply to us either.
If it is said: There must be a relation between the Creator and the created, and if the relation is actualized, then it is by a finite or infinite duration.
We say: Rather, it is necessary to negate the relation between the Creator and the created, for if the relation were actualized by a finite or infinite duration, His existence would be temporal, subject to change and motion. Is it not that if someone said: 'What is the relation of one of us where he came to be, having a beginning?' the question would be absurd. Is it not that if someone said: 'What is the relation of the world from Him, exalted, where it came to be, having an end? Is it by separation or adjacency? And if by separation, is it by a distance [؟] or a separation that is finite or infinite?' the question would be absurd. Similarly, we say regarding duration: for the particular is like the universal, and time is like space.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer. The Dahriyya argue that if the world is created (presupposing it began to exist), its existence must be delayed relative to God, and that delay must either be by a duration or not. If not by a duration, the world coexists with God eternally, which is impossible for an originated thing. If by a duration, that duration is either finite (implying God's existence also has an end) or infinite (implying an infinite number of past events, which they argue is impossible). The author refutes this by first denying the premise that 'delay' is temporal: temporal categories do not apply to God. God is not subject to time, so the division into durations is invalid. Then the author distinguishes between temporal delay and ontological priority: the Creator is the giver of existence, the created is the recipient; the Creator has no beginning, the created does. This is the correct meaning of 'delay'. Then a further question arises: if there is a relation between Creator and created, it must be by a finite or infinite duration. The author responds by denying any such relation, because a temporal relation would make God temporal and mutable. The author uses an analogy: asking about the spatial relation between God and the world is absurd, just as asking about the temporal relation is absurd. The particular is like the universal, and time is like space in this respect.

محدث
تأخر
مدة
متناهية
غير متناهية

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The Dahriyya argue that the concept of a created world inevitably leads to one of three absurdities, thereby denying creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Dahriyya's argument seems logical, but it relies on a false assumption. Are there any assumptions in your own faith that you hold without realizing they might be flawed? What would it take for you to examine them honestly?
?
This objection is a shubha (doubt) that has been answered by scholars. Do you actively seek to understand and resolve doubts about your faith, or do you avoid them? What is one step you can take this week to strengthen your conviction in God's transcendence?

Refuting the Dahriyya: God Is Beyond Time and Space
Author refutes the Dahriyya by denying temporal categories for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the Dahriyya's argument by denying that temporal categories apply to God and by distinguishing temporal delay from ontological priority.

Core Idea
God is not subject to time; thus the Dahriyya's division into durations is invalid.

In response to the Dahriyya's objection, the author first points out a fundamental flaw: they assume that God's existence is temporal. But God, being the Creator, is beyond time and space. The author then shows that the intended meaning of 'delay' is ontological priority, not temporal. This lesson examines the author's careful refutation and the analogy with spatial categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer
Read the full Arabic of the author's response. Note that it is divided into three parts: critique of formulation, denial of temporal categories, and response to the further question.
2
Understand the denial of temporal categories
The author states that temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity are impossible for God. Therefore the entire division into durations is irrelevant. Reflect on why this is a powerful move.
The author also uses an analogy: just as God is not above in place, He is not prior in time.
3
Grasp the ontological meaning
The author clarifies that the real meaning of 'delay' is that the Creator is the giver of existence and the created is the recipient. This is a logical, not temporal, priority.
4
Analyze the spatial analogy
The author draws a parallel between time and space: asking about temporal relation is as absurd as asking about spatial relation. Consider why this analogy is effective.

The Dahriyya raise an objection saying: If you say that the world is temporally originated after it was not, then its existence is delayed from the existence of God, exalted. Then it is inevitable either that it is delayed by a duration or not by a duration. If it is delayed not by a duration, then its existence coexisted with the existence of God, exalted. And if it is delayed by a duration, then it is inevitable either that it is delayed by a finite duration or by an infinite duration. If it is delayed by a finite duration, then the finitude of God's existence is necessitated. And if it is delayed by an infinite duration, then we suppose in that duration existents without end, for if a duration without end is not impossible, then a number without end is not impossible.
The answer: We say: This speech is not sound in formulation and division. As for the formulation: your saying 'if the world is temporally originated, its existence was delayed' – if you mean by it temporal delay, it is not granted, for we have already demonstrated that temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity are impossible with respect to God, exalted. And on this basis, the division into it being delayed by a duration or not by a duration does not apply to us, because that which does not accept duration in essence and existence cannot be said to be prior, posterior, or coexistent with a duration or not with a duration. So you have foisted upon us temporal priority, posteriority, and simultaneity for God, exalted. Rather, the existence of God, exalted, is not said to be prior in time, just as it is not said to be above in place, nor is it said to be coexistent in time, just as it is not said to be adjacent to the world in place. And if you mean by delay in existence, i.e., the Creator is the bestower of existence and the created is the recipient of existence, and the Creator has no beginning to His existence, and the created has a beginning, then it is granted, and the division into it being delayed by a duration or not by a duration does not apply to us either.
If it is said: There must be a relation between the Creator and the created, and if the relation is actualized, then it is by a finite or infinite duration.

Is it not that if someone said: 'What is the relation of one of us where he came to be, having a beginning?' the question would be absurd. And if by separation, is it by a distance [؟] or a separation that is finite or infinite?' the question would be absurd. Similarly, we say regarding duration: for the particular is like the universal, and time is like space.

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer. The Dahriyya argue that if the world is created (presupposing it began to exist), its existence must be delayed relative to God, and that delay must either be by a duration or not. If not by a duration, the world coexists with God eternally, which is impossible for an originated thing. If by a duration, that duration is either finite (implying God's existence also has an end) or infinite (implying an infinite number of past events, which they argue is impossible). This is the correct meaning of 'delay'. Then a further question arises: if there is a relation between Creator and created, it must be by a finite or infinite duration. The author responds by denying any such relation, because a temporal relation would make God temporal and mutable. The author uses an analogy: asking about the spatial relation between God and the world is absurd, just as asking about the temporal relation is absurd. The particular is like the universal, and time is like space in this respect.

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
6 min
God Beyond Time: Denying Temporal Relation
Author denies temporal relations and answers objection of necessary ratio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God cannot be described with temporal categories like priority, posteriority, or concomitance, and how the author refutes the objection that a temporal ratio must exist between God and creation.

Core Idea
God is free from time just as He is free from space.

In this passage, the author addresses a key challenge to divine transcendence: if God is not temporally prior to the world, does that force a temporal concomitance? He argues that denying temporal relations does not imply simultaneity, because God is beyond time altogether. Then he answers the objection that there must be a ratio (nisbah) between Creator and creation, using analogies from space to show its absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the dialectical structure: the author states his position, anticipates an objection, and answers it.
The author uses a very rigorous dialectical style.
2
Identify the three temporal relations denied
The author denies 'progression, regression, and temporal concomitance' for God. Understand what each means and why they are denied.
These are all temporal categories.
3
Understand the objection and the analogy
The objection claims a necessary ratio between creator and created. The author rejects it using analogies from space: asking about a temporal ratio is as absurd as asking about spatial separation or adjacency.
The key move: time is like space in this context.
4
Reflect on the implication for God's transcendence
Consider how this argument upholds God's absolute otherness and freedom from all created categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقدمًا وتأخرًا ومعية زمانية للباري تعالى، وإذا منعنا ذلك ألزمتم علينا مقارنة في الوجود وذلك تلبيس، فإنا إذا منعنا التقدم والتأخر الزماني منعنا المقارنة الزمانية، بل وجود الباري تعالى لا يقال: متقدم بالزمان، كما لا يقال أيضا: فوق بالمكان، ولا يقال: مقارن بالزمان كما لا يقال: مجاور للعالم بالمكان، وإن عنيتم بالتأخر في الوجود؛ أي الموجد مفيد الوجود، والموجد مستفيد الوجود، والموجد لا أول لوجوده، والموجد له أول فهو مسلم، ولا يصح أيضًا بنا التقسيم عليه أنه تأخر بمدة أو لا بمدة. فإن قيل: لا بد من نسبة ما بين الموجد والموجد، وإذا تحققت النسبة فبمدة متناهية أو غير متناهية. قلنا ولا بد من نفي النسبة بين الموجد والموجد؛ إذ لو تحققت النسبة بمدة متناهية أو غير متناهية كان وجوده زمانيًا قابلا للتغير والحركة، أليس لو قال القائل: ما نسبة واحد منا حيث حدث، وله أول كان السؤال محالا، أليس لو قال القائل: ما نسبة العالم منه تعالى حيث وجد وله نهاية أفيباينه أو يجاوره، فإن باينه أفبخلا أو بينونة تتناهى أم لا تتناهى، كان السؤال محالا، كذلك نقول في المدة فإن الجزئي كالكلي والزمان كالمكان.
Progression, regression, and temporal concomitance for God the Exalted. And if we deny that, you force upon us concomitance in existence, and that is obfuscation. For if we deny temporal progression and regression, we deny temporal concomitance. Rather, the existence of God the Exalted is not said to be temporally prior, just as it is not said to be spatially above, nor is it said to be temporally concomitant just as it is not said to be spatially adjacent to the world. And if you mean by 'regression in existence' that the creator is the bestower of existence, and the created is the receiver of existence, and the creator has no beginning to its existence, and the created has a beginning, then that is conceded. Nor is it valid for us to divide it as being regression by a duration or not by a duration. For it is said: There must be a relation between the creator and the created, and if the relation is realized, then by a finite duration or an infinite duration. We say: The relation between the creator and the created must be denied, because if the relation by a finite or infinite duration were realized, His existence would be temporal, subject to change and motion. Indeed, if someone were to say: 'What is the relation of one of us when he came to be, and he has a beginning?' the question would be absurd. Indeed, if someone were to say: 'What is the relation of the world from Him, the Exalted, when it came to be and it has an end? Is it separate from Him or adjacent to Him? If it is separate, is it by a void or a separation that is finite or infinite?' the question would be absurd. Similarly we say concerning duration: the particular is like the universal, and time is like space.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical unit: the author states his position, an objection is raised, and he provides an answer. He begins by affirming that God has no temporal attributes of progress, regress, or concomitance. If these are denied, the opponent accuses the author of positing a simultaneous existence of the world with God. The author calls this 'talbis' (obfuscation). He clarifies that denying temporal relations does not force a temporal concomitance; rather, God is free from all temporal categories, just as He is free from spatial categories like 'above' or 'adjacent'. He then concedes that if by 'regression' one means the causal relationship (the creator bestows existence, the created receives it, the creator is eternal, the created originated), that is acceptable, but it is not a temporal division of 'by a duration or not'. The objection follows: there must be some ratio (nisbah) between creator and creation, and that ratio must be either by a finite or infinite duration. The author answers by denying any such ratio. If a temporal ratio existed, God would be subject to change and motion, which is impossible. He illustrates with analogies: asking about a temporal ratio between God and the world is as absurd as asking about a spatial relation (is the world separate from God by a finite or infinite void? or adjacent?). Such questions are nonsense. Similarly, time (duration) is like space: particular durations are like specific spaces, and time as a whole is like space as a whole. Therefore, the objection fails.

Key Terms
مقدم
متأخر
معية
موجد
مستفيد
نسبة
مدة
زمان
مكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that denying God's temporal priority forces the world to be co-eternal with God (temporal concomitance).
Correction: The author denies both temporal priority and concomitance; God is beyond time entirely, so no temporal relation applies.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to show the absurdity of asking about a temporal ratio between God and the world?
A) The analogy of a particular and a universal
B) The analogy of space and spatial relations
C) The analogy of cause and effect
D) The analogy of finite and infinite

Key Takeaway
God transcends time and space, so no temporal or spatial relation can be attributed to Him, making the objection of a necessary ratio invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if God is bound by your timeline—delaying repentance, thinking you have 'time'—or do you truly believe He is beyond time and your next breath is not guaranteed? What would change today if you acted on that belief?
?
The author says asking about a temporal relation between God and the world is as absurd as a spatial relation. Have you ever mentally pictured God as 'far' or 'near' in a physical sense, or thought of His actions as happening in sequence like ours? How can you train yourself to think of God as completely beyond time and space in your worship?

If God is not 'patient' in a temporal sense (since He is beyond time), but His mercy is eternal, how does that reshape your view of your sins and His forgiveness? Do you still delay turning to Him because you assume He is waiting in your timeline?

Analyzing the Meaning of Time
Author analyzes 'muddah' into three categories and refutes each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how analyzing the term 'time' into three categories (real existent, estimated, pure non-being) refutes the opponent's claim that the relation must be by a finite or infinite time.

Core Idea
Time's meaning collapses three ways — none support a temporal gap before creation.

In this passage, the author takes on the opponent's division of time into finite or infinite by first asking: what does 'time' even mean? By examining three possibilities — real existent, mere estimation, or pure non-being — he shows that each fails to establish time as something that could exist before the world. This is a clever linguistic and logical move that dissolves the objection at its root.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Get a sense of the argument.
2
Identify the three possible meanings
Find where the author divides 'muddah' into three categories: existent, estimated, or pure non-being. Notice the phrasing.
3
Understand the refutation for each case
Follow the argument for each category: if real existent, it must be part of the world; if estimated, infinite possibilities cannot be actualized as a whole; if pure non-being, finitude/infinitude don't apply.
4
See why this undermines the opponent's division
Reflect on how the tripartite analysis shows that time cannot be something that exists before the world, making the opponent's division irrelevant.
This ties the lesson together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب آخر عن التقسيم نقول: ما المعنى بالمدة؛ أهي عبارة عن أمر موجود أو عن تقدير موجود أم عن عدم بحت؟ فإن كان أمرًا موجودًا محققا فهو من العالم فلا يكون قبل العالم، وأيضا الموجود إما قايم بنفسه أو قايم بغيره، وعلى الوجهين جميعاً لا يمكن تقديره قبل العالم، وإن كان أمرًا مقدرًا وجوده، والتقديرات الوهمية تجویزات، وليس كلما يجوزه العقل أو يقدره الوهم يمكن وجوده جملة حاصلة، فإن وجود عالم آخر، وكذلك إلى ما لا يتناهى مما يجوز يقدره الوهم، وكذلك الأعداد التي لا تتناهى مما يقدره الوهم إلا مما يجوزه العقل). وبالجملة الجايزات كلها لا يمكن أن توجد جملة حاصلة، فيكون ما لا يتناهى مما يحصره الوجود وذاك محال، فعلم أن تقدير أزمنة غير متناهية لا يكون كالتحقيق، وما يمكن وجوده جملة معًا أو متعاقباً لا يمكن أن يكون مشحونًا بما لا يتناهى، وإن كانت المدة عبارة عن عدم بحت فلا يتناهى ولا لا يتناهى في عدم البحث.
And another answer concerning the division: We say: What is meant by 'time'? Is it an expression for an existent thing, or for an estimated thing, or for pure non-being? If it is a real existent, then it is from the world, so it cannot be before the world. Also, the existent is either self-subsistent or subsistent in another, and in both cases it cannot be supposed before the world. And if it is an estimated thing whose existence is estimated, then estimative suppositions are mere possibilities, and not everything that the intellect deems possible or the imagination estimates can exist as a collective whole. For example, the existence of another world, and likewise ad infinitum, of what the imagination deems possible and estimates, as well as numbers that are infinite, which the imagination estimates but the intellect deems possible. In short, all possible things cannot exist as a collective whole, for what is infinite cannot be encompassed by existence, and that is impossible. Thus it is known that the estimation of infinite times is not like actual existence, and what can exist together or successively cannot be filled with what is infinite. And if 'time' is an expression for pure non-being, then there is no finitude or infinitude in pure non-being.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a second answer to the objection that the relation must be by a finite or infinite time. The author examines the term 'muddah' (time/duration) by dividing it into three possibilities: (1) a real existent (amr mawjud muhaqqaq), (2) an estimated thing (taqdir mawjud), or (3) pure non-being ('adam baht). He argues that if time is a real existent, it must be part of the world, so it cannot be prior to the world. Moreover, any existent is either self-subsistent (qaim bi nafsihi) or subsistent in another (qaim bi ghayrihi); in neither case can it be posited before the world. If time is merely an estimated thing (a mental construct), then estimative suppositions (takhayyulat) are mere possibilities (jawazat), and not everything the intellect or imagination can conceive can actually exist as a collective whole. The example of infinite worlds or infinite numbers shows that possibilities cannot all be actualized simultaneously or even successively in a finite framework. Thus, infinite durations cannot be actualized as a collection. If time is pure non-being, then questions of finitude or infinitude do not apply. Therefore, the opponent's division into finite or infinite time is baseless.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that infinite time in estimation implies actual infinite time.
Correction: The author insists that estimative possibility does not entail actual existence as a collective whole; infinite possibilities cannot be actualized together.

Key Takeaway
The analysis of 'time' shows that the opponent's division into finite or infinite time is meaningless because time itself cannot be posited before the world.

Refuting that Finite Time Implies Finite God
Author refutes the claim that finite time implies finite existence of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the finitude of time does not imply the finitude of God, and how the author uses the principle of 'no proportion' to defend divine transcendence.

Core Idea
God's existence is not bound by time or space; there is no proportion between Creator and creation.

In this passage, the author delivers a decisive rebuttal to an objection that tries to limit God by the world's temporality. He exposes the reasoning as circular and draws a powerful analogy with space. The key insight is that God transcends all categories of creation, so the world's finitude tells us nothing about God's nature. Let's see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the opponent's claim
Identify what the opponent is asserting: that if time is finite, God's existence must be finite. Then read the translation carefully.
2
Understand the accusation of circular reasoning
The author calls this a 'musadara' (petitio principii). Why? Because it assumes what needs to be proved: that God's existence is connected to time. Reflect on why this is fallacious.
The opponent's premise already implies the conclusion.
3
Analyze the analogy with space
The author says the finitude of the world in space does not limit God. Why? Because there is no proportion (munasaba) between God and spatial things. Apply the same reasoning to time.
4
Consider the rhetorical question
The author questions the opponent's assumption that infinite time would necessarily produce actual existents. This further weakens their position.
This challenges the opponent's underlying assumption about time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب آخر: لِمَ قلتم: إن المدة لو كانت متناهية لتناهى وجود الباري تعالى، فإن تناهي المدة كتناهي العالم مكانًا وهو مصادرة على المطلوب الأول، وتعبير عن محل النزاع، ثم تناهي العالم مكانًا ليس يقتضي تناهي ذات الباري تعالى؛ لأنه لا مناسبة بينه وبين المكانيات والمكان، كذلك تناهي العالم زمانًا لا يقتضي تناهي وجود الباري؛ لأنه لا مناسبة بينه وبين الزمانيات والزمان؟ ولِمَ قلتم: إن المدة لو لم تكن متناهية في التقدير العقلي أمكن أن يوجد فيها موجودات في التحقيق الحسي؟
And another answer: Why do you say that if time were finite, then the existence of God the Exalted would be finite? For the finitude of time is like the finitude of the world in space, and that is a petitio principii on the first demand, and an expression of the point of dispute. Moreover, the finitude of the world in space does not necessitate the finitude of the essence of God the Exalted, because there is no proportion between Him and spatial things and space. Likewise, the finitude of the world in time does not necessitate the finitude of the existence of God, because there is no proportion between Him and temporal things and time. And why do you say that if time were not finite in intellectual estimation, then existents could come to exist in it in sensory actualization?
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a third answer to the same objection. The author directly addresses the opponent's implication: if the world's duration (muddah) is finite, then God's existence would also be finite. He calls this a 'musadara' (petitio principii, circular reasoning) because the conclusion (that God's existence is finite) is assumed in the premise (that the world's time is finite). He then draws an analogy: the world's finitude in space does not entail that God's essence is spatially limited, because there is no 'munasaba' (proportion, commensurability) between God and spatial entities or space itself. Similarly, the world's finitude in time does not limit God, as there is no proportion between God and temporal things or time. The author then poses a rhetorical question: why do they claim that if time were infinite in intellectual estimation, then actual existents could come to exist in it? This implies that the opponent's assumption is also unsupported. Thus, the objection's reasoning is flawed on multiple counts.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the world is finite in time, then God must also be finite because He is related to the world.
Correction: The author argues that there is no proportion (munasaba) between God and created time or space; thus, the finitude of the world does not imply finitude of God.

Checkpoint

A) Straw man
B) Circular reasoning (petitio principii)
C) False analogy

Key Takeaway
The finitude of the world in time does not limit God's existence because God transcends all categories of creation and has no proportion with time or space.

Refuting the Link Between Finite Duration and Finite Creator
The author refutes that a finite duration entails a finite Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the finitude of the world in duration does not necessitate the finitude of God's existence, based on the principle that God is beyond spatial and temporal relations.

Core Idea
God's transcendence breaks any causal link between created finitude and divine finitude.

The opponent argues that if duration is finite, then God's existence must be finite. The author responds with a powerful analogy: just as the world's spatial finitude does not make God spatially finite, its temporal finitude does not make God temporally finite. The key is that God has no relation (munasaba) to space or time. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author structures his refutation.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Find the statement that the opponent makes: 'If duration were finite, then the existence of God would be finite.' Underline it.
3
Understand the analogy with place
The author compares finitude of duration to finitude of place. He argues that just as spatial finitude of the world does not affect God, temporal finitude also does not. The reason: 'la munasaba' (no relation).
Think about why this analogy is effective.
4
Reflect on the second objection
The author challenges another claim: that infinite duration in intellect would imply actual existents. Consider why mental estimation does not guarantee sensory reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و جواب آخر : لِمَ قلتم : إن المدة لو كانت متناهية لتناهى وجود الباري تعالى، فإن تناهي المدة كتناهي العالم مكانًا وهو مصادرة على المطلوب الأول، وتعبير عن محل النزاع، ثم تناهي العالم مكانًا ليس يقتضي تناهي ذات الباري تعالى؛ لأنه لا مناسبة بينه وبين المكانيات والمكان، كذلك تناهي العالم زمانًا لا يقتضي تناهي وجود الباري ؛ لأنه لا مناسبة بينه وبين الزمانيات والزمان؟ ولِمَ قلتم : إن المدة لو لم تكن متناهية في التقدير العقلي أمكن أن يوجد فيها موجودات في التحقيق الحسي؟
And another answer: Why do you say: If duration were finite, then the existence of God Most High would be finite? For the finitude of duration is like the finitude of the world in place, and that is an assumption of the first demand and an expression of the point of contention. Then, the finitude of the world in place does not necessitate the finitude of the essence of God Most High, because there is no relation between Him and spatial things and space.
